style="text-align:center;border-top:#aaa 1px solid"><a href="/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_state_symbols" title="Lists of United States state symbols">Lists of United States state symbols</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Rhode Island</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\xcb\x8c</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: \'o\' in \'code\'">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'tide\'">a\xc9\xaa</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\xc9\x99</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Rhode_Island.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a>\xc2\xa0</span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/En-us-Rhode_Island.ogg" title="En-us-Rhode Island.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> officially the <b>State of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-9">[9]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> region of the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">northeastern United States</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">smallest in area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">eighth least populous</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states by population density">second most densely populated</a> of the 50 U.S. states. Its official name is also the longest of any state in the Union. Rhode Island is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> to the north and east, and the Atlantic Ocean to the south via <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Sound" title="Rhode Island Sound">Rhode Island Sound</a> and <a href="/wiki/Block_Island_Sound" title="Block Island Sound">Block Island Sound</a>. It also shares a small maritime border with <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The state capital and most populous city in Rhode Island is <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a>.</p>\n<p>On May 4, 1776, the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Colony of Rhode Island</a> became the first of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> to renounce its allegiance to the British Crown,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and it was the fourth among the newly independent states to ratify the <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">Articles of Confederation</a> on February 9, 1778.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The state boycotted the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(United_States)" title="Constitutional Convention (United States)">1787 convention</a> which drew up the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and initially refused to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ratify" title="Ratify">ratify</a> it;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> it was the last of the original states to do so, on May 29, 1790.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island\'s official nickname is "The Ocean State", a reference to the large bays and inlets that amount to about 14% of its total area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-area_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-area-2">[2]</a></sup> Rhode Island covers 1,214 square miles (3,144\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>), of which 1,045 square miles (2,707\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>) are land.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctext">Professional</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-44"><a href="#Collegiate_and_amateur_sports"><span class="tocnumber">13.8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Collegiate and amateur sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Landmarks"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Landmarks</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Notable_people"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-50"><a href="#Primary_sources"><span class="tocnumber">18.1</span> <span class="toctext">Primary sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-51"><a href="#Secondary_sources"><span class="tocnumber">18.2</span> <span class="toctext">Secondary sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_name">Origin of the name</span></h2>\n<p>Despite its name, most of Rhode Island is located on the mainland of the United States. Its official name is <i>State of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations</i>, which is derived from the merger of four Colonial settlements. The settlements of <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Rhode_Island" title="Portsmouth, Rhode Island">Portsmouth</a> were situated on what is commonly called <a href="/wiki/Aquidneck_Island" title="Aquidneck Island">Aquidneck Island</a> today, but it was called <i>Rhode Island</i> in Colonial times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portsmouth_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-portsmouth-18">[18]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Providence_Plantations" title="Providence Plantations">Providence Plantation</a></i> was the name of the colony founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Williams_(theologian)" title="Roger Williams (theologian)">Roger Williams</a> in the area now known as the city of <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-water_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-water-19">[19]</a></sup> This was adjoined by the settlement of <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="Warwick, Rhode Island">Warwick</a>; hence the plural Providence Plantations.</p>\n<p>It is unclear how Aquidneck Island came to be known as <i>Rhode Island</i>, but two historical events may have influenced the name.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Explorer <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">Giovanni da Verrazzano</a> noted the presence of an island near the mouth of Narragansett Bay in 1524 which he likened to the island of <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a> (part of modern Greece).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Subsequent European explorers were unable to precisely identify the island that Verrazzano had named, but the Pilgrims who later colonized the area assumed that it was Aquidneck.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Adriaen_Block" title="Adriaen Block">Adriaen Block</a> passed by Aquidneck during his expeditions in the 1610s, and he described it in a 1625 account of his travels as "an island of reddish appearance," which was "<i>een rodlich Eylande</i>" in 17th-century Dutch, and one popular notion is that this Dutch phrase might have influenced the name Rhode Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> (Historians have theorized that this "reddish appearance" resulted from either red autumn foliage or red clay on portions of the shore.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Verrazzano_monument.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="276" data-file-width="574" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Verrazzano_monument.jpg/220px-Verrazzano_monument.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Verrazzano_monument.jpg/330px-Verrazzano_monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Verrazzano_monument.jpg/440px-Verrazzano_monument.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Verrazzano_monument.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nVerrazzano Monument, Providence, Rhode Island.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The earliest documented use of the name "Rhode Island" for Aquidneck was in 1637 by Roger Williams. The name was officially applied to the island in 1644 with these words: "Aquethneck shall be henceforth called the Isle of Rodes or Rhode-Island." The name "Isle of Rodes" is used in a legal document as late as 1646.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Dutch maps as early as 1659 call the island "Red Island" (<i>Roodt Eylant</i>).</p>\n<p>Roger Williams was a theologian who was forced out of the Massachusetts Bay Colony, seeking religious and political tolerance. He and others founded Providence Plantation as a free proprietary colony. "Providence" referred to the concept of <a href="/wiki/Divine_providence" title="Divine providence">divine providence</a>, and "plantation" was an English <a href="/wiki/Plantation_(settlement_or_colony)" title="Plantation (settlement or colony)">term for a colony</a>. "State of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations" is the longest official name of any state in the Union.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_contestation_of_the_name">2009 contestation of the name</span></h3>\n<p>In recent years, the presence of the word <i>plantation</i> in the state\'s name became a sufficiently contested issue that the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_General_Assembly" title="Rhode Island General Assembly">General Assembly</a> voted on June 25, 2009 to hold a general referendum determining whether "and Providence Plantations" would be dropped from the official name. Advocates for excising <i>plantation</i> asserted that the word symbolized an alleged legacy of native disenfranchisement for many Rhode Islanders, as well as the proliferation of slavery in the colonies and in the post-colonial United States. (Rhode Island abolished slavery in 1652, but the law was not enforced and, by the early 18th century, it was "the epicenter of the North American slave trade", according to the <i>Brown Daily Herald</i>.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wootton_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-wootton-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beacon_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-beacon-28">[28]</a></sup> Advocates for retaining the name argued that <i>plantation</i> was simply an archaic synonym for <i><a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a></i> and bore no relation to slavery. The referendum election was held on November 2, 2010, and the people voted overwhelmingly (78% to 22%) to retain the entire original name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of counties in Rhode Island">List of counties in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_New_England" title="Geology of New England">Geology of New England</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_-_NED500.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="337" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Rhode_Island_-_NED500.jpg/170px-Rhode_Island_-_NED500.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Rhode_Island_-_NED500.jpg/255px-Rhode_Island_-_NED500.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ed/Rhode_Island_-_NED500.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_-_NED500.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTerrain map of Rhode Island</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Rhode Island covers an area of 1,214 square miles (3,144\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>) located within the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> Region, and is bordered on the north and east by <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, on the west by <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, and on the south by <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Sound" title="Rhode Island Sound">Rhode Island Sound</a> and the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-area_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-area-2">[2]</a></sup> It shares a narrow maritime border with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State" title="New York State">New York State</a> between Block Island and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>. The mean elevation of the state is 200 feet (61\xc2\xa0m). It is only 37 miles (60\xc2\xa0km) wide and 48 miles (77\xc2\xa0km) long, yet the state has a tidal shoreline on Narragansett Bay and the Atlantic Ocean of 384 miles (618\xc2\xa0km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island is <a href="/wiki/Nickname" title="Nickname">nicknamed</a> the Ocean State and has a number of oceanfront <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_beaches_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of beaches in Rhode Island">beaches</a>. It is mostly flat with no real mountains, and the state\'s highest natural point is <a href="/wiki/Jerimoth_Hill" title="Jerimoth Hill">Jerimoth Hill</a>, 812 feet (247\xc2\xa0m) above sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgs_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-usgs-31">[31]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island has two distinct natural regions. Eastern Rhode Island contains the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lowland" title="Lowland">lowlands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Narragansett_Bay" title="Narragansett Bay">Narragansett Bay</a>, while Western Rhode Island forms part of the New England Upland. Rhode Island\'s forests are part of the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_coastal_forests" title="Northeastern coastal forests">Northeastern coastal forests</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecoregions_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecoregions-32">[32]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Narragansett Bay is a major feature of the state\'s topography. There are more than 30 islands within the bay. The largest is <a href="/wiki/Aquidneck_Island" title="Aquidneck Island">Aquidneck Island</a>, shared by the municipalities of Newport, Middletown, and Portsmouth. The second-largest island is <a href="/wiki/Conanicut_Island" title="Conanicut Island">Conanicut</a>; the third-largest is <a href="/wiki/Prudence_Island" title="Prudence Island">Prudence</a>. <a href="/wiki/Block_Island" title="Block Island">Block Island</a> lies about 12 miles (19\xc2\xa0km) off the southern coast of the mainland and separates <a href="/wiki/Block_Island_Sound" title="Block Island Sound">Block Island Sound</a> and the Atlantic Ocean proper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A rare type of rock called <a href="/wiki/Cumberlandite" title="Cumberlandite">Cumberlandite</a> is found only in Rhode Island (specifically in the town of <a href="/wiki/Cumberland,_Rhode_Island" title="Cumberland, Rhode Island">Cumberland</a>) and is the state rock. There were initially two known deposits of the mineral, but it is an ore of iron and one of the deposits was extensively mined for its ferrous content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<table style="background:transparent;margin-top:0.5em;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto">\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;font-weight:bold">Geography of Rhode Island</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<table style="width:180px;float:left;border-collapse:collapse;margin:3px">\n<tr>\n<td style="height:190px;border:1px solid Island\xc2\xa0</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_taxa_described_from_Rhode_Island" title="List of taxa described from Rhode Island">List of taxa described from Rhode Island</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="527" data-file-width="800" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg/220px-Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg/330px-Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg/440px-Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blackstone-River-Bikeway.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe Blackstone River Greenway in autumn, approximately one mile (1.6 km) south of the Martin St. Bridge</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Most of Rhode Island has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>, with warm summers and cold winters. The far southern and coastal portions of the state are the broad transition zone into <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climate</a> or subtropical climates, with hot summers and cool winters with a mix of rain and snow. The highest temperature recorded in Rhode Island was 104\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (40\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), recorded on August 2, 1975 in Providence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The lowest recorded temperature in Rhode Island was \xe2\x88\x9223\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9231\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on February 5, 1996 in <a href="/wiki/Greene,_Rhode_Island" title="Greene, Rhode Island">Greene</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Monthly average temperatures range from a high of 83\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (28\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) to a low of 20\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x927\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island is vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical storms and hurricanes</a> due to its location in <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>, catching the brunt of many storms blowing up the Eastern Seaboard. Some hurricanes that have done significant damage in the state are the <a href="/wiki/1938_New_England_hurricane" title="1938 New England hurricane">1938 New England hurricane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carol" title="Hurricane Carol">Hurricane Carol</a> (1954), <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Donna" title="Hurricane Donna">Hurricane Donna</a> (1960), and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bob" title="Hurricane Bob">Hurricane Bob</a> (1991).</p>\n<div aria-labelledby="Rivers_of_Rhode_Island" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="padding:3px">\n<table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">\n<tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" scope="col">\n<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n<ul>\n<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:RIRivers" title="Template:RIRivers"><abbr style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;" title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>\n<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:RIRivers" title="Template talk:RIRivers"><abbr style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;" title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>\n<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:RIRivers&amp;action=edit"><abbr style=";;background:none style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">\n<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Annaquatucket_River" title="Annaquatucket River">Annaquatucket River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Barrington_River_(Rhode_Island)" title="Barrington River (Rhode Island)">Barrington River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hunt_River_(Rhode_Island)" title="Hunt River (Rhode Island)">Hunt River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kickamuit_River" title="Kickamuit River">Kickamuit River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maidford_River" title="Maidford River">Maidford River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maiford_River" title="Maiford River">Maiford River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maskerchugg_River" title="Maskerchugg River">Maskerchugg River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mattatuxet_River" title="Mattatuxet River">Mattatuxet River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Palmer_River_(Massachusetts_%E2%80%93_Rhode_Island)" title="Palmer River (Massachusetts \xe2\x80\x93 Rhode Island)">Palmer River</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pettaquamscutt_River" Point</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Rhode_Island" title="History of Rhode Island">History of Rhode Island</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Providence,_Rhode_Island,_Original_Deed.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="598" data-file-width="474" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/15/Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_Original_Deed.jpg/170px-Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_Original_Deed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/15/Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_Original_Deed.jpg/255px-Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_Original_Deed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/15/Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_Original_Deed.jpg/340px-Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_Original_Deed.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Providence,_Rhode_Island,_Original_Deed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe original 1636 deed to Providence, signed by <a href="/wiki/Canonicus" title="Canonicus">Chief Canonicus</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span id="Colonial_era:_1636\xe2\x80\x931770"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era:_1636.E2.80.931770">Colonial era: 1636\xe2\x80\x931770</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="352" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg/170px-First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg/255px-First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg/340px-First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_Baptist_Church_in_America_in_RI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/First_Baptist_Church_in_America" title="First Baptist Church in America">The congregation founded</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Williams_(theologian)" title="Roger Williams (theologian)">Roger Williams</a> in 1638 built this <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a> historic church in 1776</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="493" data-file-width="694" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg/220px-Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg/330px-Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg/440px-Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roger_Williams_and_Narragansetts.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nRoger Williams and Narragansett Indians</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 1636, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Williams_(theologian)" title="Roger Williams (theologian)">Roger Williams</a> was banished from the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay Colony</a> for his religious views, and he settled at the top of Narragansett Bay on land sold or given to him by Narragansett sachem <a href="/wiki/Canonicus" title="Canonicus">Canonicus</a>. He named the site <i><a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a></i>, "having a sense of God\'s merciful providence unto me in my distress."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-39">[39]</a></sup> Eventually, it became a place of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_freedom" title="Religious freedom">religious freedom</a>.</p>\n<p>In 1638 (after conferring with Williams), <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hutchinson" title="Anne Hutchinson">Anne Hutchinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Coddington" title="William Coddington">William Coddington</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Clarke_(Baptist_minister)" title="John Clarke (Baptist minister)">John Clarke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Sherman" title="Philip Sherman">Philip Sherman</a>, and other religious dissenters settled on <a href="/wiki/Aquidneck_Island" title="Aquidneck Island">Aquidneck Island</a> (then known as Rhode Island), which was purchased from the local tribes who called it Pocasset. This settlement was called <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Rhode_Island" title="Portsmouth, Rhode Island">Portsmouth</a> and was governed by the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Compact" title="Portsmouth Compact">Portsmouth Compact</a>. The southern part of the island became the separate settlement of <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a> after disagreements among the founders.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Samuel_Gorton" title="Samuel Gorton">Samuel Gorton</a> purchased lands at Shawomet in 1642 from the Narragansetts, precipitating a dispute with the Massachusetts Bay Colony. In 1644, Providence, Portsmouth, and Newport united for their common independence as the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations</a>, governed by an elected council and "president". Gorton received a separate charter for his settlement in 1648, which he named <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="Warwick, Rhode Island">Warwick</a> after his patron.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a> was founded in 1764 as the College in the English Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations. It was one of nine <a href="/wiki/Colonial_colleges" title="Colonial colleges">Colonial colleges</a> granted charters before the American Revolution, but was the first college in America to accept students regardless of religious affiliation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>\n<p>During <a href="/wiki/King_Philip%27s_War" title="King Philip\'s War">King Philip\'s War</a> (1675\xe2\x80\x931676), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wampanoag_people" title="Wampanoag people">Wampanoag</a> tribe under war-leader <a href="/wiki/Metacomet" title="Metacomet">Metacomet</a>, whom the colonists called King Philip, invaded and burned down several of the towns in the area\xe2\x80\x94including Providence, which was attacked twice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-39">[39]</a></sup> A force of Massachusetts, Connecticut, and Plymouth militia under General <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Winslow" title="Josiah Winslow">Josiah Winslow</a> invaded and destroyed the fortified Narragansett Indian village in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Swamp_Fight" title="Great Swamp Fight">Great Swamp</a> in what is now <a href="/wiki/South_Kingstown,_Rhode_Island" title="South Kingstown, Rhode Island">South Kingstown, Rhode Island</a> on December 19, 1675.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In one of the final actions of the war, an Indian associated with <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Church_(ranger)" title="Benjamin Church (ranger)">Benjamin Church</a> killed King Philip in what is now <a href="/wiki/Bristol,_Rhode_Island" title="Bristol, Rhode Island">Bristol, Rhode Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The colony was amalgamated into the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_New_England" title="Dominion of New England">Dominion of New England</a> in 1686, as <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">King James II</a> attempted to enforce royal authority over the autonomous colonies in <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> of 1688, the colony regained its independence under the Royal Charter. Slaves were introduced at this time, although there is no record of any law legalizing slave-holding. The colony later prospered under the slave trade, distilling rum to sell in Africa as part of a profitable <a href="/wiki/Triangular_trade" title="Triangular trade">triangular trade</a> in slaves and sugar with the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:King_Philip%27s_Seat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="300" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/King_Philip%27s_Seat.jpg/220px-King_Philip%27s_Seat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a6/King_Philip%27s_Seat.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:King_Philip%27s_Seat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n"<a href="/wiki/Metacomet" title="Metacomet">King Philip</a>\'s Seat", an Indian meeting place on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Hope,_(Rhode_Island)" title="Mount Hope, (Rhode Island)">Mount Hope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol,_Rhode_Island" title="Bristol, Rhode Island">Bristol, Rhode Island</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span id="Revolutionary_to_Civil_War_period:_1770\xe2\x80\x931860"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolutionary_to_Civil_War_period:_1770.E2.80.931860">Revolutionary to Civil War period: 1770\xe2\x80\x931860</span></h3>\n<p>Rhode Island\'s tradition of independence and dissent gave it a prominent role in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>. At approximately 2\xc2\xa0a.m. on June 10, 1772, a band of Providence residents <a href="/wiki/Gaspee_Affair" title="Gaspee Affair">attacked</a> the grounded revenue schooner <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HMS_Gasp%C3%A9e_(1763)" title="HMS Gasp\xc3\xa9e (1763)">Gaspee</a></i>, burning it to the waterline for enforcing <a href="/wiki/Navigation_Acts" title="Navigation Acts">unpopular trade regulations</a> within Narragansett Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Rhode Island was the first of the thirteen colonies to renounce its allegiance to the British Crown on May 4, 1776.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KnowRhode_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-KnowRhode-46">[46]</a></sup> It was also the last of the thirteen colonies to ratify the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a> on May 29, 1790, once assurances were made that a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">Bill of Rights</a> would become part of the Constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> During the Revolution, the British occupied Newport in December 1776. A combined Franco-American force fought to drive them off Aquidneck Island. Portsmouth was the site of the first African-American military unit, the <a href="/wiki/1st_Rhode_Island_Regiment" title="1st Rhode Island Regiment">1st Rhode Island Regiment</a>, to fight for the U.S. in the unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rhode_Island" title="Battle of Rhode Island">Battle of Rhode Island</a> of August 29, 1778.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> A month earlier, the appearance of a French fleet off Newport caused the British to scuttle some of their own ships in an attempt to block the harbor. The British abandoned Newport in October 1779, concentrating their forces in New York City. An <a href="/wiki/Exp%C3%A9dition_Particuli%C3%A8re" title="Exp\xc3\xa9dition Particuli\xc3\xa8re">expedition of 5,500 French troops</a> under <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Donatien_de_Vimeur,_comte_de_Rochambeau" title="Jean-Baptiste Donatien de Vimeur, comte de Rochambeau">Count Rochambeau</a> arrived in Newport by sea on July 10, 1780.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington-Rochambeau_Revolutionary_Route" title="Washington-Rochambeau Revolutionary Route">celebrated march</a> to <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">Yorktown, Virginia</a> in 1781 ended with the defeat of the British at the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Siege of Yorktown</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Chesapeake" title="Battle of the Chesapeake">Battle of the Chesapeake</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:W-RSimpleMap.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2718" data-file-width="1960" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/W-RSimpleMap.gif/170px-W-RSimpleMap.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/W-RSimpleMap.gif/255px-W-RSimpleMap.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/W-RSimpleMap.gif/340px-W-RSimpleMap.gif 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:W-RSimpleMap.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nNational Park Service map of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington-Rochambeau_Revolutionary_Route" title="Washington-Rochambeau Revolutionary Route">Washington-Rochambeau Revolutionary Route</a>, which commenced in Rhode Island.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Rhode Island was heavily involved in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> during the post-revolution era. In 1774, the slave population of Rhode Island was 6.3%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> nearly twice as high as any other New England colony<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Providence,_Rhode_Island,_1858.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="431" data-file-width="672" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_1858.jpg/220px-Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_1858.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_1858.jpg/330px-Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_1858.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_1858.jpg/440px-Providence%2C_Rhode_Island%2C_1858.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Providence,_Rhode_Island,_1858.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nProvidence in the mid-19th century</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Rhode Island was also heavily involved in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, which began in America in 1787 when <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Somers" title="Thomas Somers">Thomas Somers</a> reproduced textile machine plans which he imported from England. He helped to produce the <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Cotton_Manufactory" title="Beverly Cotton Manufactory">Beverly Cotton Manufactory</a>, in which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moses_Brown_(Providence)" title="Moses Brown (Providence)">Moses Brown</a> of Providence took an interest. Moses Brown teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Slater" title="Samuel Slater">Samuel Slater</a> and helped to create the second cotton mill in America, a water-powered textile mill. The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution#Industrial_Revolution_elsewhere" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> moved large numbers of workers into the cities, creating a permanently landless class who were therefore also voteless. By 1829, 60% of the state\'s free white males were ineligible to vote. Several attempts were unsuccessfully made to address this problem, and a new state constitution was passed in 1843 allowing landless men to vote if they could pay a $1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poll_tax_(United_States)" title="Poll tax (United States)">poll tax</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park,_Newport,_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1838" data-file-width="2265" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park%2C_Newport%2C_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg/220px-Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park%2C_Newport%2C_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park%2C_Newport%2C_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg/330px-Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park%2C_Newport%2C_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park%2C_Newport%2C_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg/440px-Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park%2C_Newport%2C_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Former_Stable_at_Brenton_Point_State_Park,_Newport,_Rhode_Island_1968.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAbandoned stables, <a href="/wiki/Brenton_Point_State_Park" title="Brenton Point State Park">Brenton Point State Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a> (1968)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>For the first several decades of statehood, Rhode Island was governed in accordance with the 1663 <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Royal_Charter" title="Rhode Island Royal Charter">colonial charter</a>. Voting rights were restricted to landowners holding at least $134 in property, disenfranchising well over half of the state\'s male citizens. The charter apportioned legislative seats equally among the state\'s towns, over-representing rural areas and under-representing the growing industrial centers. Additionally, the charter disallowed landless citizens from filing civil suits without endorsement from a landowner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Bills were periodically introduced in the legislature to expand suffrage, but they were invariably defeated. In 1841, activists led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_W._Dorr" title="Thomas W. Dorr">Thomas W. Dorr</a> organized an extralegal convention to draft a state constitution,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> arguing that the charter government violated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guarantee_Clause" title="Guarantee Clause">Guarantee Clause</a> in Article Four, Section Four of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>. In 1842, the charter government and Dorr\'s supporters held separate elections, and two rival governments claimed sovereignty over the state. Dorr\'s supporters led an armed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dorr_rebellion" title="Dorr rebellion">rebellion</a> against the charter government, and Dorr was arrested and imprisoned for treason against the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Later that year, the legislature drafted a state constitution, removing property requirements for American-born citizens but keeping them in place for immigrants, and retaining urban under-representation in the legislature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the early 19th century, Rhode Island was subject to a tuberculosis outbreak which led to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_vampire_panic" title="Rhode Island vampire panic">public hysteria about vampirism</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span></h3>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, Rhode Island was the first Union state to send troops in response to <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">President Lincoln</a>\'s request for help from the states. Rhode Island furnished 25,236 fighting men, of whom 1,685 died. On the home front, Rhode Island and the other northern states used their industrial capacity to supply the Union Army with the materials that it needed to win the war. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a> moved to Rhode Island temporarily during the war.</p>\n<p>In 1866, Rhode Island abolished racial segregation in the public schools throughout the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Gilded_Age">The Gilded Age</span></h3>\n<p>The 50 years following the Civil War were a time of prosperity and affluence that author William G. McLoughlin calls "Rhode Island\'s halcyon era." Rhode Island was a center of the <a href="/wiki/Gilded_Age" title="Gilded Age">Gilded Age</a> and provided a home or summer home to many of the country\'s most prominent industrialists. This was a time of growth in textile mills and manufacturing and brought an influx of immigrants to fill those jobs, bringing population growth and urbanization. In <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a>, New York\'s wealthiest industrialists created a summer haven to socialize and build <a href="/wiki/Preservation_Society_of_Newport_County" title="Preservation Society of Newport County">grand mansions</a>. Thousands of French-Canadian, Italian, Irish, and Portuguese immigrants arrived to fill jobs in the textile and manufacturing mills in Providence, Pawtucket, Central Falls, and Woonsocket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McLoughlin_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-McLoughlin-56">[56]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span></h3>\n<p>During World War I, Rhode Island furnished 28,817 soldiers, of whom 612 died. After the war, the state was hit hard by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Influenza" title="Spanish Influenza">Spanish Influenza</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the 1920s and 1930s, rural Rhode Island saw a surge in <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a> membership, largely in reaction to large waves of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">immigrants</a> moving to the state. The Klan is believed to be responsible for burning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watchman_Industrial_School" title="Watchman Industrial School">Watchman Industrial School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scituate,_Rhode_Island" title="Scituate, Rhode Island">Scituate</a>, which was a school for African-American children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Growth_in_the_modern_era:_1929\xe2\x80\x93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_in_the_modern_era:_1929.E2.80.93present">Growth in the modern era: 1929\xe2\x80\x93present</span></h3>\n<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, the Rhode Island <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> has dominated local politics. Rhode Island has comprehensive health insurance for low-income children and a large <a href="/wiki/Social_safety_net" title="Social safety net">social safety net</a>. Many urban areas still have a high rate of children in poverty. Due to an influx of residents from Boston, increasing housing costs have resulted in more homeless in Rhode Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="604" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg/220px-N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg/330px-N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg/440px-N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:N3419822_37931820_6163Providence.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nProvidence in 2009</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The 350th Anniversary of the founding of Rhode Island was celebrated with a free concert held on the tarmac of the Quonset State Airport on August 31, 1986. Performers included <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommy_James" title="Tommy James">Tommy James</a>, and headliner <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hope" title="Bob Hope">Bob Hope</a>.</p>\n<p>In 2003, a <a href="/wiki/The_Station_nightclub_fire" title="The Station nightclub fire">nightclub fire</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="West Warwick, Rhode Island">West Warwick</a> claimed 100 lives and resulted in nearly twice as many injured, catching national attention. The fire resulted in criminal sentences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butler_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Butler-60">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In March 2010, areas of the state received record flooding due to rising rivers from heavy rain. The first period of rainy weather in mid-March caused localized flooding and, two weeks later, more rain caused more widespread flooding in many towns, especially south of Providence. Rain totals on March 29\xe2\x80\x9330, 2010 exceeded 14\xc2\xa0inches (35.5\xc2\xa0cm) in many locales, resulting in the inundation of area rivers\xe2\x80\x94especially the Pawtuxet River which runs through central Rhode Island. The overflow of the Pawtuxet River, nearly 11 feet (3\xc2\xa0m) above flood stage, submerged a sewage treatment plant and closed a five-mile (8\xc2\xa0km) stretch of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">Interstate 95</a>. In addition, it flooded two shopping malls, numerous businesses, and many homes in the towns of Warwick, West Warwick, Cranston, and Westerly. Amtrak service was also suspended between New York and Boston during this period. Following the flood, Rhode Island was in a state of emergency for two days. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) was called in to help flood victims.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Rhode_Island" title="Government of Rhode Island">Government of Rhode Island</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin:1em; font-size:95%;">\n<caption>Gubernatorial election results<sup class="reference" The state\'s current governor is <a href="/wiki/Gina_Raimondo" title="Gina Raimondo">Gina Raimondo</a> (D), and the lieutenant governor is Daniel McKee (D). Raimondo became Rhode Island\'s first female governor with a plurality of the vote in the November 2014 state elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Its United States Senators are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jack_Reed_(politician)" title="Jack Reed (politician)">Jack Reed</a> (D) and <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Whitehouse" title="Sheldon Whitehouse">Sheldon Whitehouse</a> (D). Rhode Island\'s two United States Representatives are <a href="/wiki/David_Cicilline" title="David Cicilline">David Cicilline</a> (D-1) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jim_Langevin" title="Jim Langevin">Jim Langevin</a> (D-2). <i>See <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_congressional_districts#Rhode_Island" title="List of United States congressional districts">congressional districts map</a>.</i></p>\n<p>Rhode Island is one of a few states that do not have an official Governor\'s residence. <i>See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Rhode_Island_Governors" title="List of Rhode Island Governors">List of Rhode Island Governors</a>.</i></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States)" title="State legislature (United States)">state legislature</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_General_Assembly" title="Rhode Island General Assembly">Rhode Island General Assembly</a>, consisting of the 75-member <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_House_of_Representatives" title="Rhode Island House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> and the 38-member <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Senate" title="Rhode Island Senate">Senate</a>. Both houses of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> body are currently dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Democratic_Party" title="Rhode Island Democratic Party">Democratic Party</a>; the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Republican_Party" title="Rhode Island Republican Party">Republican Party</a> is almost non-existent in the state government, with Republicans holding a handful of seats in both the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Senate" title="Rhode Island Senate">Senate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_House_of_Representatives" title="Rhode Island House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections_in_Rhode_Island" title="Elections in Rhode Island">Elections in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island,_2016.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3201" data-file-width="2904" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island%2C_2016.svg/200px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island%2C_2016.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island%2C_2016.svg/300px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island%2C_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island%2C_2016.svg/400px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island%2C_2016.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Rhode_Island,_2016.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treemap" title="Treemap">Treemap</a> of the popular vote by county, 2016 presidential election.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Rhode Island\'s population barely crosses the threshold for additional votes in both the federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">Electoral College</a>; it is well represented relative to its population, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population" title="List of U.S. states by population">eighth-highest</a> number of electoral votes and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population" title="List of U.S. states by population">second-highest</a> number of House Representatives per resident. Based on its area, Rhode Island even has the highest density of electoral votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Federally, Rhode Island is a reliably Democratic state during presidential elections, usually supporting the Democratic Presidential nominee. The state voted for the Republican Presidential candidate until <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1908" title="United States presidential election, 1908">1908</a>. Since then, it has voted for the Republican nominee for President seven times, and the Democratic nominee 17 times. The last 16 presidential elections in Rhode Island have resulted in the Democratic Party winning the Ocean State\'s Electoral College votes 12 times. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1980" title="United States presidential election, 1980">1980 presidential election</a>, Rhode Island was one of six states to vote against <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>. Reagan was the last Republican to win any of the state\'s counties in a Presidential election until Donald Trump won Kent County in 2016. In 1988, <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> won over 40% of the state\'s popular vote, something that no Republican has done since.</p>\n<p>Rhode Island was the Democrats\' leading state in 1988 and 2000, and second-best in 1968, 1996, and 2004. Rhode Island\'s most one-sided Presidential election result was in 1964, with over 80% of Rhode Island\'s votes going for <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>. In 2004, Rhode Island gave <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> more than a 20-percentage-point margin of victory (the third-highest of any state), with 59.4% of its vote. All but three of Rhode Island\'s 39 cities and towns voted for the Democratic candidate. The exceptions were East Greenwich, West Greenwich, and Scituate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In 2008, Rhode Island gave <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> a 28-percentage-point margin of victory (the third-highest of any state), with 63% of its vote. All but one of Rhode Island\'s 39 cities and towns voted for the Democratic candidate (the exception being Scituate).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Rhode_Island" title="Political party strength in Rhode Island">Political party strength in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin:10px">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="6">Voter registration and party enrollment as of March 15, 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Party</th>\n<th>Active voters</th>\n<th>Inactive voters</th>\n<th>Total voters</th>\n<th>Percentage</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#3333FF;" width="10px"></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">259,263</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">22,586</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">286,625</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">40.97%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#E81B23;" width="10px"></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">65,033</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">6,792</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">72,613</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">10.38%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#FDFD7F;" width="10px"></td>\n<td>Unaffiliated</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">306,697</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">29,253</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">340,085</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">48.61%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Total</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">631,320</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">58,634</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">699,653</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">100%</th>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<p>Rhode Island has abolished capital punishment, making it one of 19 states that have done so. Rhode Island abolished the death penalty very early, just after <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, the first state to abolish it, and carried out its last execution in the 1840s. Rhode Island was the second to last state to make prostitution illegal. Until November 2009 Rhode Island law <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Rhode_Island" title="Prostitution in Rhode Island">made prostitution legal</a> provided it took place indoors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In a 2009 study Rhode Island was listed as the 9th safest state in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2011, Rhode Island became the third state in the United States to pass legislation to allow the use of medical marijuana. Additionally, the Rhode Island General Assembly passed civil unions, and it was signed into law by Governor <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Chafee" title="Lincoln Chafee">Lincoln Chafee</a> on July 2, 2011. Rhode Island became the eighth state to fully recognize either same-sex marriage or civil unions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Same-sex marriage became legal on May 2, 2013, and took effect August 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island has some of the highest taxes in the country, particularly its property taxes, ranking seventh in local and state taxes, and sixth in real estate taxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taxes_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-taxes-72">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<table class="toccolours" style="border-spacing: 1px; float: right; clear: style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">Source: 1910\xe2\x80\x932010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><br/>\n2015 estimate<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-74">[74]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_population_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Rhode_Island_population_map.png/220px-Rhode_Island_population_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Rhode_Island_population_map.png/330px-Rhode_Island_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Rhode_Island_population_map.png/440px-Rhode_Island_population_map.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_population_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nRhode Island Population Density Map</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Rhode Island was 1,056,298 on July 1, 2015, a 0.35% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Rhode Island is located in <a href="/wiki/Providence_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence County, Rhode Island">Providence County</a>, in the city of <a href="/wiki/Cranston,_Rhode_Island" title="Cranston, Rhode Island">Cranston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> A corridor of population can be seen from the Providence area, stretching northwest following the <a href="/wiki/Blackstone_River" title="Blackstone River">Blackstone River</a> to <a href="/wiki/Woonsocket,_Rhode_Island" title="Woonsocket, Rhode Island">Woonsocket</a>, where 19th-century mills drove industry and development.</p>\n<p>According to the 2010 Census, 81.4% of the population was White (76.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_white" title="Non-Hispanic white">non-Hispanic white</a>), 5.7% was Black or African American, 0.6% American Indian and Alaska Native, 2.9% Asian, 0.1% Native Hawaiian and other Pacific Islander, 3.3% from two or more races. 12.4% of the total population was of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> or Latino origin (they may be of any race).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">\n<caption>Rhode Island racial breakdown of population</caption>\n<tr>\n<th>Racial composition</th>\n<th>1970<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-77">[77]</a></sup></th>\n<th>1990<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-census-77">[77]</a></sup></th>\n<th>2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></th>\n<th>2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">Black</a></td>\n<td>2.7%</td>\n<td>3.9%</td>\n<td>4.5%</td>\n<td>5.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian and<br/>\n<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">other Pacific Islander</a></td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>0.1%</td>\n<td>0.1%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Other race</a></td>\n<td>0.2%</td>\n<td>2.5%</td>\n<td>5.0%</td>\n<td>6.1%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a></td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>2.7%</td>\n<td>3.3%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Of the people residing in Rhode Island, 58.7% were born in Rhode Island, 26.6% were born in a different state, 2.0% were born in Puerto Rico, U.S. Island areas or born abroad to American parent(s), and 12.6% were foreign born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to the U.S. Census Bureau, as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rhode_Island&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Rhode Island had an estimated population of 1,056,298, which is an increase of 1,125, or 0.10%, from the prior year and an increase of 3,731, or 0.35%, since the year 2010. This includes a natural increase since the last census of 15,220 people (that is 66,973 births minus 51,753 deaths) and an increase due to net migration of 14,001 people into the state. <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">Immigration</a> from outside the United States resulted in a net increase of 18,965 people, and migration within the country produced a net decrease of 4,964 people.</p>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanics_in_the_United_States" title="Hispanics in the United States">Hispanics</a> in the state make up 12.8% of the population, predominantly Dominican, Puerto Rican, and Guatemalan populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_U.S._Census" title="2000 U.S. Census">2000 U.S. Census</a>, 84% of the population aged 5 and older spoke only <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>, while 8.07% spoke Spanish at home, 3.80% Portuguese, 1.96% French, 1.39% Italian and 0.78% speak other languages at home accordingly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The state\'s most populous ethnic group, non-Hispanic white, has declined from 96.1% in 1970 to 76.5% in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In 2011, 40.3% of Rhode Island\'s children under the age of one belonged to racial or ethnic minority groups, meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<p>6.1% of Rhode Island\'s population were reported as under 5, 23.6% under 18, and 14.5% were 65 or older. Females made up approximately 52% of the population.</p>\n<p>According to the 2010\xe2\x80\x932015 <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a>, the largest ancestry groups were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> (18.3%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> (18.0%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> (10.5%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_American" title="French American">French</a> (10.4%), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_American" title="Portuguese American">Portuguese</a> (9.3%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island has a higher percentage of Americans of Portuguese ancestry, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_American" title="Portuguese American">Portuguese Americans</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_American" title="Cape Verdean American">Cape Verdean Americans</a> than any other state in the nation. Additionally, the state also has the highest percentage of <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberian</a> immigrants, with more than 15,000 residing in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Italian Americans make up a plurality in central and southern Providence County and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French-Canadian_Americans" title="French-Canadian Americans">French-Canadian Americans</a> form a large part of northern Providence County. Irish Americans have a strong presence in Newport and Kent counties. Americans of English ancestry still have a presence in the state as well, especially in <a href="/wiki/Washington_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Washington County, Rhode Island">Washington County</a>, and are often referred to as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swamp_Yankees" title="Swamp Yankees">Swamp Yankees</a>." African immigrants, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_American" title="Cape Verdean American">Cape Verdean Americans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberian_American" title="Liberian American">Liberian Americans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nigerian_American" title="Nigerian American">Nigerian Americans</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghanaian_American" title="Ghanaian American">Ghanaian Americans</a>, form significant and growing communities in Rhode Island.</p>\n<p>Although Rhode Island has the smallest land area of all 50 states, it has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states by population density">second highest population density</a> of any state in the Union, second to that of New Jersey.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_data">Birth data</span></h3>\n<p><i>Note: Births in table don\'t add up, because Hispanics are counted both by their ethnicity and by their race, giving a higher overall number.</i></p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Live Births by Race/Ethnicity of Mother</caption>\n<tr>\n<th><a hidden;">\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">23%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other Christian</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:grey; width:2%; overflow: hidden;">\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em;
