hidden;">\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.5%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Islam</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:green; width:0.5%; overflow: hidden;">\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.5%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1571" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg/170px-Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg/255px-Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg/340px-Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grace_Episcopal_Church_Providence_2017.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Grace_Church_(Providence,_Rhode_Island)" title="Grace Church (Providence, Rhode Island)">Grace Church</a>, a historic church at 175 Mathewson Street in <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence, Rhode Island</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>A Pew survey of Rhode Island residents\' religious self-identification showed the following distribution of affiliations: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">Roman Catholic</a> 43%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> 27%, <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">Jewish</a> 1%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Eastern_Orthodox_Church_in_North_America" title="History of the Eastern Orthodox Church in North America">Orthodox</a> 1%, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> 1%, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_the_United_States" title="Buddhism in the United States">Buddhism</a> 1%, <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a> 0.5%, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_United_States" title="Hinduism in the United States">Hinduism</a> 0.5%, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_United_States" title="Islam in the United States">Islam</a> 0.5% and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-religious" title="Non-religious">Non-religious</a> 23%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The largest denominations are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> with 456,598 adherents, the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal Church</a> with 19,377, the <a href="/wiki/American_Baptist_Churches_USA" title="American Baptist Churches USA">American Baptist Churches USA</a> with 15,220, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> with 6,901 adherents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-92">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island has one of the highest proportions of Roman Catholic residents of any state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catholic_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-catholic-93">[93]</a></sup> mainly due to large Irish, Italian, and French-Canadian immigration in the past; recently, significant Portuguese and various Hispanic communities have also been established in the state. Though it has one of the highest overall Catholic percentages of any state, none of Rhode Island\'s individual counties ranks among the 10 most Catholic in the United States, as Catholics are very evenly spread throughout the state.</p>\n<p>The Jewish community of Rhode Island is centered in the Providence area, and emerged during a wave of Jewish immigration predominately from Eastern Europeans <a href="/wiki/Shtetl" title="Shtetl">shtetls</a> between 1880 and 1920. The presence of the <a href="/wiki/Touro_Synagogue" title="Touro Synagogue">Touro Synagogue</a> in Newport, the oldest existing synagogue in the United States, emphasizes that these second-wave immigrants did not create Rhode Island\'s first Jewish community; a comparatively smaller wave of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_and_Portuguese_Jews" title="Spanish and Portuguese Jews">Spanish and Portuguese Jews</a> immigrated to Newport during the colonial era.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_towns">Cities and towns</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of municipalities in Rhode Island">List of municipalities in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Rhode Island locations by per capita income">Rhode Island locations by per capita income</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Villages_in_Rhode_Island" title="Category:Villages in Rhode Island">Category:Villages in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<p>Rhode Island is divided into <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of counties in Rhode Island">five counties</a> but it has no county governments. The entire state is divided into municipalities, which handle all local government affairs.</p>\n<p>There are 39 cities and towns in Rhode Island. Major population centers today result from historical factors; development took place predominantly along the <a href="/wiki/Blackstone_River" title="Blackstone River">Blackstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seekonk_River" title="Seekonk River">Seekonk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Providence_River" title="Providence River">Providence Rivers</a> with the advent of the water-powered mill. Providence is the base of a large metropolitan area.</p>\n<p>The state\'s 15 largest municipalities ranked by population are:</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">\n<ol>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a> (178,042)<sup class="reference" (22,954)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhode_Island_populations_100-7"><a href="#cite_note-Rhode_Island_populations-100">[100]</a></sup></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n<p>Some of Rhode Island\'s cities and towns are further partitioned into villages, in common with many other New England states. Notable villages include <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Rhode_Island" title="Kingston, Rhode Island">Kingston</a> in the town of South Kingstown, which houses the University of Rhode Island; <a href="/wiki/Wickford,_Rhode_Island" title="Wickford, Rhode Island">Wickford</a> in the town of North Kingstown, the site of an annual international art festival; and <a href="/wiki/Wakefield,_Rhode_Island" title="Wakefield, Rhode Island">Wakefield</a> where the Town Hall is located for the Town of South Kingstown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerycaption">Major Cities of Rhode Island</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: href="/wiki/Bristol,_Rhode_Island" title="Bristol, Rhode Island">Bristol</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg/220px-Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg/330px-Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg/440px-Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newport_Rhode_Island_USA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA historic side street in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Rhode Island locations by per capita income">Rhode Island locations by per capita income</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Providencetextronside.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Providencetextronside.JPG/220px-Providencetextronside.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Providencetextronside.JPG/330px-Providencetextronside.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Providencetextronside.JPG/440px-Providencetextronside.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Providencetextronside.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Textron_Tower" title="Textron Tower">Textron\'s headquarters</a>, in the company of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_Financial_Plaza" title="One Financial Plaza">One Financial Plaza</a> and the Rhode Island Hospital Trust building.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RI_towns_Narragansett.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="604" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/RI_towns_Narragansett.png/220px-RI_towns_Narragansett.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/RI_towns_Narragansett.png/330px-RI_towns_Narragansett.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/RI_towns_Narragansett.png/440px-RI_towns_Narragansett.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RI_towns_Narragansett.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/The_Towers_(Narragansett,_Rhode_Island)" title="The Towers (Narragansett, Rhode Island)">Narragansett Towers</a> and Narragansett Town Beach, one of Rhode Island\'s tourist destinations.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Rhode Island economy had a colonial base in fishing.</p>\n<p>The Blackstone River Valley was a major contributor to the <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_United_States" title="Economic history of the United States">American</a> Industrial Revolution. It was in <a href="/wiki/Pawtucket,_Rhode_Island" title="Pawtucket, Rhode Island">Pawtucket</a> that <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Slater" title="Samuel Slater">Samuel Slater</a> set up <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slater_Mill" title="Slater Mill">Slater Mill</a> in 1793,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> using the waterpower of the <a href="/wiki/Blackstone_River" title="Blackstone River">Blackstone River</a> to power his <a href="/wiki/Cotton_mill" title="Cotton mill">cotton mill</a>. For a while, Rhode Island was one of the leaders in textiles. However, with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, most textile factories relocated to southern US states. The textile industry still constitutes a part of the Rhode Island economy but does not have the same power that it once had.</p>\n<p>Other important industries in Rhode Island\'s past included toolmaking, <a href="/wiki/Costume_jewelry" title="Costume jewelry">costume jewelry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cutlery" title="Cutlery">silverware</a>. An interesting by-product of Rhode Island\'s industrial history is the number of abandoned factories, many of them now being used for condominiums, museums, offices, and low-income and elderly housing. Today, much of the economy of Rhode Island is based in services, particularly healthcare and education, and still manufacturing to some extent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The state\'s nautical history continues in the 21st century in the form of nuclear submarine construction.</p>\n<p>Per the 2013 American Communities Survey, Rhode Island has the highest paid elementary school teachers in the country, with an average salary of $75,028 (adjusted to inflation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Financial_Group" title="Citizens Financial Group">Citizens Financial Group</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a>, the 14th largest bank in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The Fortune 500 companies <a href="/wiki/CVS_Caremark" title="CVS Caremark">CVS Caremark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Textron" title="Textron">Textron</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Woonsocket,_Rhode_Island" title="Woonsocket, Rhode Island">Woonsocket</a> and Providence, respectively. <a href="/wiki/FM_Global" title="FM Global">FM Global</a>, <a href="/wiki/GTECH_Corporation" title="GTECH Corporation">GTECH Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Power_Conversion" title="American Power Conversion">American Power Conversion</a>, Nortek, and <a href="/wiki/Amica_Mutual_Insurance" title="Amica Mutual Insurance">Amica Mutual Insurance</a> are all Fortune 1000 companies that are based in Rhode Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island\'s 2000 total gross state production was $46.18 billion (adjusted to inflation), placing it 45th in the nation. Its 2000 <i>per capita</i> personal income was $41,484 (adjusted to inflation), 16th in the nation. Rhode Island has the lowest level of energy consumption per capita of any state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Additionally, Rhode Island is rated as the 5th most energy efficient state in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In December 2012, the state\'s unemployment rate was 10.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Health services are Rhode Island\'s largest industry. Second is tourism, supporting 39,000 jobs, with tourism-related sales at $4.56 billion (adjusted to inflation) in the year 2000. The third-largest industry is manufacturing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Its industrial outputs are submarine construction, shipbuilding, costume jewelry, fabricated metal products, electrical equipment, machinery, and boatbuilding. Rhode Island\'s agricultural outputs are nursery stock, vegetables, dairy products, and eggs.</p>\n<p>Rhode Island\'s taxes were appreciably higher than neighboring states,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taxes_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-taxes-72">[72]</a></sup> because Rhode Island\'s income tax was based on 25% of the payer\'s federal income tax payment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Former Governor Donald Carcieri claimed that the higher tax rate had an inhibitory effect on business growth in the state and called for reductions to increase the competitiveness of the state\'s business environment. In 2010, the Rhode Island General Assembly passed a new state income tax structure that was then signed into law on June 9, 2010 by Governor Carcieri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The income tax overhaul has now made Rhode Island competitive with other New England states by lowering its maximum tax rate to 5.99% and reducing the number of tax brackets to three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The state\'s first income tax was enacted in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_employers">Largest employers</span></h3>\n<p>As of March 2011, the largest employers in Rhode Island (excluding navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Department_of_Transportation" title="Rhode Island Department of Transportation">Rhode Island Department of Transportation</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg/220px-RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg/330px-RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg/440px-RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIPTA_Gillig_Low_Floor_0517.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA RIPTA bus at <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Plaza" title="Kennedy Plaza">Kennedy Plaza</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Public_Transit_Authority" title="Rhode Island Public Transit Authority">Rhode Island Public Transit Authority</a> (RIPTA) operates statewide intra- and intercity bus transport from its hubs at <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Plaza" title="Kennedy Plaza">Kennedy Plaza</a> in Providence, <a href="/wiki/Pawtucket,_Rhode_Island" title="Pawtucket, Rhode Island">Pawtucket</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a>. RIPTA bus routes serve 38 of Rhode Island\'s 39 cities and towns. (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Shoreham,_Rhode_Island" title="New Shoreham, Rhode Island">New Shoreham</a> on <a href="/wiki/Block_Island" title="Block Island">Block Island</a> is not served). RIPTA currently operates 58 routes, including daytime trolley service (using trolley-style replica buses) in Providence and Newport.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferry">Ferry</span></h3>\n<p>From 2000 through 2008, RIPTA offered seasonal ferry service linking Providence and Newport (already connected by highway) funded by grant money from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Transportation" title="United States Department of Transportation">United States Department of Transportation</a>. Though the service was popular with residents and tourists, RIPTA was unable to continue on after the federal funding ended. Service was discontinued as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rhode_Island&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The service was resumed in 2016 and has been successful. The privately run Block Island Ferry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> links <a href="/wiki/Block_Island" title="Block Island">Block Island</a> with <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Narragansett,_Rhode_Island" title="Narragansett, Rhode Island">Narragansett</a> with traditional and fast-ferry service, while the Prudence Island Ferry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> connects <a href="/wiki/Bristol,_Rhode_Island" title="Bristol, Rhode Island">Bristol</a> with <a href="/wiki/Prudence_Island" title="Prudence Island">Prudence Island</a>. Private ferry services also link several Rhode Island communities with ports in <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, and New York. The Vineyard Fast Ferry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> offers seasonal service to <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha\'s Vineyard">Martha\'s Vineyard</a> from <a href="/wiki/Quonset_Point" title="Quonset Point">Quonset Point</a> with bus and train connections to Providence, Boston, and New York. Viking Fleet<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> offers seasonal service from Block Island to <a href="/wiki/New_London,_Connecticut" title="New London, Connecticut">New London, Connecticut</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montauk,_New_York" title="Montauk, New York">Montauk, New York</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/MBTA_Commuter_Rail" title="MBTA Commuter Rail">MBTA Commuter Rail</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Providence/Stoughton_Line" title="Providence/Stoughton Line">Providence/Stoughton Line</a> links Providence and <a href="/wiki/T._F._Green_Airport" title="T. F. Green Airport">T. F. Green Airport</a> with Boston. The line was later extended southward to <a href="/wiki/Wickford_Junction_(MBTA_station)" title="Wickford Junction (MBTA station)">Wickford Junction</a>, with service beginning April 23, 2012. The state hopes to extend the MBTA line to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingston_Railroad_Station_(Rhode_Island)" title="Kingston Railroad Station (Rhode Island)">Kingston</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westerly_(Amtrak_station)" title="Westerly (Amtrak station)">Westerly</a>. as well as explore the possibility of extending Connecticut\'s <a href="/wiki/Shore_Line_East" title="Shore Line East">Shore Line East</a> to T.F. Green Airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Amtrak\'s <a href="/wiki/Acela_Express" title="Acela Express">Acela Express</a> stops at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Providence_Station" title="Providence Station">Providence Station</a> (the only Acela stop in Rhode Island), linking Providence to other cities in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a>. Amtrak\'s <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Northeast Regional</a> service makes stops at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Providence_Station" title="Providence Station">Providence Station</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingston_Railroad_Station_(Rhode_Island)" title="Kingston Railroad Station (Rhode Island)">Kingston</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westerly_(Amtrak_station)" title="Westerly (Amtrak station)">Westerly</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation">Aviation</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Aviation_in_Rhode_Island" title="Aviation in Rhode Island">Aviation in Rhode Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of airports in Rhode Island">List of airports in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<p>Rhode Island\'s primary airport for passenger and cargo transport is <a href="/wiki/T._F._Green_Airport" title="T. F. Green Airport">T. F. Green Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="Warwick, Rhode Island">Warwick</a>, though most Rhode Islanders who wish to travel internationally on direct flights and those who seek a greater availability of flights and destinations often fly through <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Logan International Airport</a> in Boston.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Limited_access_highways">Limited access highways</span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Rhode_Island" title="Interstate 95 in Rhode Island">Interstate 95</a> runs southwest to northeast across the state, linking Rhode Island with other states along the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_295_(Rhode_Island-Massachusetts)" title="Interstate 295 (Rhode Island-Massachusetts)">Interstate 295</a> functions as a partial <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">beltway</a> encircling Providence to the west. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_195_(Rhode_Island_%E2%80%93_Massachusetts)" title="Interstate 195 (Rhode Island \xe2\x80\x93 Massachusetts)">Interstate 195</a> provides a limited-access highway connection from Providence (and <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> and New York via I-95) to Cape Cod. Initially built as the easternmost link in the (now cancelled) extension of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_84_(east)" title="Interstate 84 (east)">Interstate 84</a> from <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a>, a portion of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_6_in_Rhode_Island" title="U.S. Route 6 in Rhode Island">U.S. Route 6</a> through northern Rhode Island is limited-access and links I-295 with downtown Providence.</p>\n<p>Several Rhode Island highways extend the state\'s limited-access highway network. <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_4" title="Rhode Island Route 4">RI-4</a> is a major north-south freeway linking Providence and <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="Warwick, Rhode Island">Warwick</a> (via I-95) with suburban and beach communities along <a href="/wiki/Narragansett_Bay" title="Narragansett Bay">Narragansett Bay</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_10" title="Rhode Island Route 10">RI-10</a> is an urban <a href="/wiki/Connector_(road)" title="Connector (road)">connector</a> linking downtown Providence with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cranston_(RI)" title="Cranston (RI)">Cranston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johnston,_Rhode_Island" title="Johnston, Rhode Island">Johnston</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_37" title="Rhode Island Route 37">RI-37</a> is an important east-west freeway through Cranston and Warwick and links I-95 with I-295. <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_99" title="Rhode Island Route 99">RI-99</a> links <a href="/wiki/Woonsocket,_Rhode_Island" title="Woonsocket, Rhode Island">Woonsocket</a> with Providence (via <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_146" title="Rhode Island Route 146">RI-146</a>). <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_146" title="Rhode Island Route 146">RI-146</a> travels through the <a href="/wiki/Blackstone_Valley" title="Blackstone Valley">Blackstone Valley</a>, linking Providence and I-95 with <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">Worcester, Massachusetts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Turnpike" title="Massachusetts Turnpike">Massachusetts Turnpike</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_403" title="Rhode Island Route 403">RI-403</a> links RI-4 with <a href="/wiki/Quonset_Point" title="Quonset Point">Quonset Point</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg/220px-Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg/330px-Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg/440px-Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge" title="Claiborne Pell Newport Bridge">Claiborne Pell Newport Bridge</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Several bridges cross <a href="/wiki/Narragansett_Bay" title="Narragansett Bay">Narragansett Bay</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Aquidneck_Island" title="Aquidneck Island">Aquidneck Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conanicut_Island" title="Conanicut Island">Conanicut Island</a> to the mainland, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Claiborne_Pell_Newport_Bridge" title="Claiborne Pell Newport Bridge">Claiborne Pell Newport Bridge</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamestown-Verrazano_Bridge" title="Jamestown-Verrazano Bridge">Jamestown-Verrazano Bridge</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle_paths">Bicycle paths</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/East_Bay_Bike_Path" title="East Bay Bike Path">East Bay Bike Path</a> stretches from Providence to Bristol along the eastern shore of Narragansett Bay, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackstone_River_Bikeway" title="Blackstone River Bikeway">Blackstone River Bikeway</a> will eventually link Providence and Worcester. In 2011, Rhode Island completed work on a marked on-road bicycle path through Pawtucket and Providence, connecting the <a href="/wiki/East_Bay_Bike_Path" title="East Bay Bike Path">East Bay Bike Path</a> with the Blackstone River Bikeway, completing a 33.5 miles (54\xc2\xa0km) bicycle route through the eastern side of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/William_C._O%27Neill_Bike_Path" title="William C. O\'Neill Bike Path">William C. O\'Neill Bike Path</a> (commonly known as the South County Bike Path) is an 8-mile (13\xc2\xa0km) path through South Kingstown and Narragansett. The 14-mile (22.5\xc2\xa0km) <a href="/wiki/Washington_Secondary_Rail_Trail" title="Washington Secondary Rail Trail">Washington Secondary Bike Path</a> stretches from Cranston to Coventry, and the 2-mile (3\xc2\xa0km) <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ten_Mile_River_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ten Mile River Greenway (page does not exist)">Ten Mile River Greenway</a> path runs through East Providence and Pawtucket.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span></h2>\n<p>On May 29, 2014, Governor Lincoln D. Chafee announced that Rhode Island was one of eight states to release a collaborative Action Plan to put 3.3 million zero emission vehicles on the roads by 2025. The goal of the plan is to reduce greenhouse gas and smog-causing emissions. The Action Plan covers promoting zero emission vehicles and investing in the infrastructure to support them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2014, Rhode Island received grants from the Environmental Protection Agency in the amount of $2,711,685 to clean up Brownfield sites in eight locations. The intent of the grants was to provide communities with the funding necessary to assess, clean up, and redevelop contaminated properties, boost local economies, and leverage jobs while protecting public health and the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2013, the "Lots of Hope" program was established in the City of Providence to focus on increasing the city\'s green space and local food production, improve urban neighborhoods, promote healthy lifestyles and improve environmental sustainability. "Lots of Hope" supported by a $100,000 grant will partner with the City of Providence, the Soutside Community Land Trust and the Rhode Island Foundation to convert city-owned vacant lots into productive urban farms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2012, Rhode Island passed bill S2277/H7412, "An act relating to Health and Safety \xe2\x80\x93 Environmental Cleanup Objectives for Schools", informally known as the "School Siting Bill." The bill, sponsored by Senator Juan Pichardo and Representative Scott Slater and signed into law by the Governor, made Rhode Island the first state in the US to prohibit school construction on Brownfield Sites where there is an ongoing potential for toxic vapors to negatively impact indoor air quality. It also creates a public participation process whenever a city or town considers building a school on any other kind of contaminated site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Rhode_Island" title="Media in Rhode Island">Media in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg/440px-BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/University_Hall_(Brown_University)" title="University Hall (Brown University)">University Hall</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a> is one of the oldest academic buildings in the United States.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Histor1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Histor1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBello Center at <a href="/wiki/Bryant_University" title="Bryant University">Bryant University</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_schools">Primary and secondary schools</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_schools" title="Rhode Island schools">Rhode Island schools</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of colleges and universities in Rhode Island">List of colleges and universities in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<p>Rhode Island has several colleges and universities:</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bryant_University" title="Bryant University">Bryant University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Community_College_of_Rhode_Island" title="Community College of Rhode Island">Community College of Rhode Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Wales_University" title="Johnson &amp; Wales University">Johnson &amp; Wales University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Naval_War_College" title="Naval War College">Naval War College</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/New_England_Institute_of_Technology" title="New England Institute of Technology">New England Institute of Technology</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Providence_College" title="Providence College">Providence College</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_College" title="Rhode Island College">Rhode Island College</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_School_of_Design" href="/wiki/Salve_Regina_University" title="Salve Regina University">Salve Regina University of Newport</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Rhode_Island" title="University of Rhode Island">University of Rhode Island</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_accent">Local accent</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beavertailwater.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Beavertailwater.jpg/220px-Beavertailwater.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Beavertailwater.jpg/330px-Beavertailwater.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Beavertailwater.jpg/440px-Beavertailwater.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beavertailwater.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBeavertail State Park</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG/220px-Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG/330px-Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG/440px-Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Redwood_Library_Newport.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Redwood_Library_and_Athenaeum" title="Redwood Library and Athenaeum">Redwood Library and Athenaeum</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Some Rhode Islanders speak with the distinctive, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhotic_and_non-rhotic_accents" title="Rhotic and non-rhotic accents">non-rhotic</a>, traditional <a href="/wiki/New_England_English#Southeastern_New_England" title="New England English">Rhode Island accent</a> that many compare to a cross between the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_English" title="New York City English">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_accent" title="Boston accent">Boston accents</a> (e.g., "water" sounds like "watuh"). Many Rhode Islanders distinguish a strong <i>aw</i> sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[\xc9\x94\xc9\x99]</span> (i.e., do not exhibit the <a href="/wiki/Cot%E2%80%93caught_merger" title="Cot\xe2\x80\x93caught merger">cot\xe2\x80\x93caught merger</a>) as one might hear in New Jersey or New York City; for example, the word <i>coffee</i> is pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[\xcb\x88k\xca\xb0\xc9\x94\xc9\x99fi]</span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>KAW</b>-fee</i></small></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rilang_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-rilang-133">[133]</a></sup> This type of accent may have been brought to the region by early settlers from eastern England in the Puritan migration to New England in the mid-17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Islanders refer to a drinking fountain as a "bubbler" (sometimes pronounced "bubahluh") and sometimes call milkshakes "cabinets". A foot-long, overstuffed sandwich (of whatever kind) is called a "grinder."</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_beverages">Food and beverages</span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rhode_Island&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(December 2013)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Several foods and dishes are unique to Rhode Island and some are hard to find outside of the state. <a href="/wiki/Hot_wiener" title="Hot wiener">Hot wieners</a> are sometimes called gaggers, weinies, or New York System wieners, and they are smaller than a standard hot dog, served covered in a meat sauce, chopped onions, <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">mustard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Celery_salt" title="Celery salt">celery salt</a>. Famous to Rhode Island is <a href="/wiki/Snail" title="Snail">Snail Salad</a>, which is served at numerous restaurants throughout the state. The dish is normally prepared "family style" with over five pounds of snails mixed in with other ingredients commonly found in seafood dishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> <i>Grinders</i> are submarine sandwiches, with a popular version being the Italian grinder, which is made with cold cuts (usually ham, <a href="/wiki/Prosciutto" title="Prosciutto">prosciutto</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capicola" title="Capicola">capicola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salami" title="Salami">salami</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provolone_cheese" title="Provolone cheese">Provolone cheese</a>). <a href="/wiki/Lingui%C3%A7a" title="Lingui\xc3\xa7a">Lingui\xc3\xa7a</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chouri%C3%A7o" title="Chouri\xc3\xa7o">chouri\xc3\xa7o</a> (a spicy Portuguese sausage) and peppers is also popular among the state\'s large Portuguese community, eaten with hearty bread (though this is also popular in other areas of New England).</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Pizza_strips" title="Pizza strips">Pizza strips</a> are prepared in Italian bakeries and sold in most supermarkets and convenience stores. They are rectangular strips of pizza without cheese. Their rich flavor comes solely from a dense, zesty tomato paste baked on a half-inch (1.3\xc2\xa0cm) thick pan pizza crust, and may be enjoyed warm or cold. Party pizza is a box of these pizza strips. Spinach pies are similar to a calzone but filled with seasoned spinach instead of meat, sauce, and cheese. Variations can include black olives or pepperoni with the spinach.</p>\n<p>As in colonial times, <a href="/wiki/Johnnycake" title="Johnnycake">johnnycakes</a> are made with corn meal and water, then pan-fried much like pancakes. During fairs and carnivals, Rhode Islanders enjoy dough boys, plate-sized disks of <a href="/wiki/Fried_dough" title="Fried dough">fried dough</a> sprinkled with powdered sugar (or pizza sauce). <a href="/wiki/Zeppole" title="Zeppole">Zeppole</a> are Italian doughnut-like pastries traditionally eaten on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph\'s Day">Saint Joseph\'s Day</a>, often made with exposed centers of vanilla pudding, cream filling, or <a href="/wiki/Ricotta" title="Ricotta">ricotta</a> cream, and sometimes topped with a cherry.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Waterplacepark.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Waterplacepark.JPG/220px-Waterplacepark.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Waterplacepark.JPG/330px-Waterplacepark.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Waterplacepark.JPG/440px-Waterplacepark.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Waterplacepark.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nWaterplace Park in Providence</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>As in many coastal states, seafood is readily available. <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">Shellfish</a> is extremely popular, with clams being used in multiple ways. The <a href="/wiki/Hard_clam" title="Hard clam">quahog</a> is a large local clam usually used in a chowder. (The word <i>quahog</i> comes from the Narragansett Indian word "poquauhock"; see <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Key_into_the_Language_of_America" title="A Key into the Language of America">A Key into the Language of America</a></i> by Roger Williams 1643.) It is also ground and mixed with stuffing (and sometimes spicy minced sausage) and then baked in its shell to form a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stuffie" title="Stuffie">stuffie</a></i>. Steamed clams are also a very popular dish. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calamari" title="Calamari">Calamari</a> (squid) is sliced into rings and fried and is served as an appetizer in most Italian restaurants, typically Sicilian-style (i.e., tossed with sliced banana peppers and with marinara sauce on the side).</p>\n<p>Rhode Island, like the rest of New England, has a tradition of <a href="/wiki/Clam_chowder" title="Clam chowder">clam chowder</a>. Both the white New England variety and the red Manhattan variety are popular, but there is also a unique clear-broth chowder known as <i>Rhode Island Clam Chowder</i> available in many restaurants. According to <a href="/wiki/Good_Eats" title="Good Eats">Good Eats</a>, the addition of tomatoes in place of milk was initially the work of Portuguese immigrants in Rhode Island, as tomato-based stews were already a traditional part of Portuguese cuisine, and milk was costlier than tomatoes. Scornful New Englanders called this modified version "Manhattan-style" clam chowder because, in their view, calling someone a New Yorker was an insult.</p>\n<p>A culinary tradition in Rhode Island is the <i><a href="/wiki/Clam_cake" title="Clam cake">clam cake</a></i> (also known as a clam fritter outside of Rhode Island), a deep fried ball of buttery dough with chopped bits of clam inside. They are sold by the half-dozen or dozen in most seafood restaurants around the state. The quintessential summer meal in Rhode Island is chowder and clam cakes.</p>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clams_Casino" title="Clams Casino">Clams Casino</a> originated in Rhode Island after being invented by Julius Keller, the maitre d\' in the original Casino next to the seaside Towers in Narragansett.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gourmet_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gourmet-136">[136]</a></sup> Clams Casino resemble the beloved stuffed quahog but are generally made with the smaller littleneck or cherrystone clam and are unique in their use of bacon as a topping.</p>\n<p>According to a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Providence_Journal" title="Providence Journal">Providence Journal</a></i> article, the state features both the highest number and highest density of coffee/doughnut shops per capita in the country, with 342 coffee/doughnut shops in the state. At one point, <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts" title="Dunkin\' Donuts">Dunkin\' Donuts</a> alone had over 225 locations;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> as of December 2013, there are still more than 175 Dunkin\' Donuts shops within the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The official state drink of Rhode Island is <i><a href="/wiki/Coffee_milk" title="Coffee milk">coffee milk</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> a beverage created by mixing milk with coffee syrup. This unique syrup was invented in the state and is sold in almost all Rhode Island supermarkets, as well as border states. Coffee milk contains some caffeine, yet it is sold in school cafeterias throughout the state. Strawberry milk is also as popular as chocolate milk.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_Rhode_Islanders">Famous Rhode Islanders</span></h3>\n<table class="infobox mw-collapsible marker</a></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_3.svg" title="Rhode Island state route marker"><img alt="Rhode Island state route
