symbols</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Famous_people_from_Rhode_Island" title="Famous people from Rhode Island">Famous people from Rhode Island</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Low_numbered_license_plates">Low numbered license plates</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ocean_State_512.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="517" data-file-width="1029" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ocean_State_512.jpg/220px-Ocean_State_512.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ocean_State_512.jpg/330px-Ocean_State_512.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ocean_State_512.jpg/440px-Ocean_State_512.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ocean_State_512.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAn example of a "low" three digit license plate</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_Rhode_Island" title="Vehicle registration plates of Rhode Island">Vehicle registration plates of Rhode Island</a></div>\n<p>Politicians have distributed low-numbered license plates since 1904 (when the first black and white porcelain plates were issued by the state) as a way to reward supporters or associates. Such plates have become a status symbol, similar to the culture surrounding low-numbered plates in Delaware.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> State officials made Rhode Island one of the few states to allow the owner to transfer license plates to other family members in their will.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Additionally, an official license plate lottery was implemented in 1995 through the Governor\'s Office<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> for "preferred plates".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> A plate\'s value depends on its category, with the traditional "Ocean State" legend plate (or "wave plate") being the most valuable. The Division of Motor Vehicles also allows a motorist to choose the two letters at the beginning of the plate serial, provided that such a combination is available on-hand and is not considered a "preferred plate".</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="377" data-file-width="500" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg/220px-Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg/330px-Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg/440px-Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_Summer_Homes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSome Rhode Islanders have second "summer homes" by the coast.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_in_popular_culture" title="Rhode Island in popular culture">Rhode Island in popular culture</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Farrelly_brothers" title="Farrelly brothers">Farrelly brothers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seth_MacFarlane" title="Seth MacFarlane">Seth MacFarlane</a> depict Rhode Island in popular culture, often making comedic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parodies" title="Parodies">parodies</a> of the state. MacFarlane\'s television series <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i> is based in a fictional Rhode Island city named Quahog, and notable local events and celebrities are regularly lampooned. <a href="/wiki/Peter_Griffin" title="Peter Griffin">Peter Griffin</a> is seen working at the Pawtucket <a href="/wiki/Brewery" title="Brewery">brewery</a>, and other state locations are mentioned.</p>\n<p>The movie <i><a href="/wiki/High_Society_(1956_film)" title="High Society (1956 film)">High Society</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Bing_Crosby" title="Bing Crosby">Bing Crosby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grace_Kelly" title="Grace Kelly">Grace Kelly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a>) was set in Newport, Rhode Island.</p>\n<p>The 1974 film adaptation of <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Gatsby" title="The Great Gatsby">The Great Gatsby</a> was also filmed in Newport.</p>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Bouvier_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Bouvier Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline Bouvier</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> were married at St. Mary\'s church in Newport. Their reception was held at <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Farm" title="Hammersmith Farm">Hammersmith Farm</a>, the Bouvier summer home in Newport.</p>\n<p>Cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Don_Bousquet" title="Don Bousquet">Don Bousquet</a>, a state icon, has made a career out of Rhode Island culture, drawing Rhode Island-themed gags in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Providence_Journal" title="The Providence Journal">The Providence Journal</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Yankee_(magazine)" title="Yankee (magazine)">Yankee</a></i> magazine. These cartoons have been reprinted in the <i>Quahog</i> series of paperbacks (<i>I Brake for Quahogs</i>, <i>Beware of the Quahog</i>, and <i>The Quahog Walks Among Us</i>.) Bousquet has also collaborated with humorist and <i>Providence Journal</i> columnist <a href="/wiki/Mark_Patinkin" title="Mark Patinkin">Mark Patinkin</a> on two books: <i>The Rhode Island Dictionary</i> and <i>The Rhode Island Handbook</i>.</p>\n<p>The 1998 film <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_Joe_Black" title="Meet Joe Black">Meet Joe Black</a></i> was filmed at <a href="/wiki/Aldrich_Mansion" title="Aldrich Mansion">Aldrich Mansion</a> in the Warwick Neck area of <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="Warwick, Rhode Island">Warwick</a>.</p>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Body_of_Proof" title="Body of Proof">Body of Proof</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'</span>s first season was filmed entirely in Rhode Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The show premiered on March 29, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The 2007 <a href="/wiki/Steve_Carell" title="Steve Carell">Steve Carell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dane_Cook" title="Dane Cook">Dane Cook</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Dan_in_Real_Life" title="Dan in Real Life">Dan in Real Life</a></i> was filmed in various coastal towns in the state. The sunset scene with the entire family on the beach takes place at <a href="/wiki/Napatree_Point" title="Napatree Point">Napatree Point</a>.</p>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Jersey_Shore_(TV_series)" title="Jersey Shore (TV series)">Jersey Shore</a></i> star Pauly D filmed part of his spin-off <i>The Pauly D Project</i> in his hometown of Johnston.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a> cable television series <i><a href="/wiki/Another_Period" title="Another Period">Another Period</a></i> is set in Newport during the <a href="/wiki/Gilded_Age" title="Gilded Age">Gilded Age</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_firsts_in_Rhode_Island">Famous firsts in Rhode Island</span></h3>\n<p>Rhode Island has been the first in a number of initiatives. The <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations</a> enacted the first law prohibiting <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> in North America on May 18, 1652.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Slater Mill in Pawtucket was the first commercially successful cotton-spinning mill with a fully mechanized power system in America and was the birthplace of the Industrial Revolution in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The oldest Fourth of July Parade in the country is still held annually in <a href="/wiki/Bristol,_Rhode_Island" title="Bristol, Rhode Island">Bristol, Rhode Island</a>. The first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist_Church" title="Baptist Church">Baptist Church</a> in America was founded in Providence in 1638.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ann_Smith_Franklin" title="Ann Smith Franklin">Ann Smith Franklin</a> of the Newport <i>Mercury</i> was the first female newspaper editor in America (August 22, 1762).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Touro_Synagogue" title="Touro Synagogue">Touro Synagogue</a> was the first synagogue in America, founded in Newport in 1763.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-2"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The first act of armed rebellion in America against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Crown" title="British Crown">British Crown</a> was the boarding and burning of the Revenue Schooner <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaspee" title="Gaspee">Gaspee</a></i> in Narragansett Bay on June 10, 1772. The idea of a <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a> was first proposed at a town meeting in Providence on May 17, 1774. Rhode Island elected the first delegates (<a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hopkins_(politician)" title="Stephen Hopkins (politician)">Stephen Hopkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Ward_(American_statesman)" title="Samuel Ward (American statesman)">Samuel Ward</a>) to the Continental Congress on June 15, 1774. The Rhode Island General Assembly created the first standing army in the colonies (1,500 men) on April 22, 1775. On June 15, 1775, the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval" title="Naval">naval</a> engagement of the American Revolution occurred between a Colonial Sloop commanded by Capt. <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Whipple" title="Abraham Whipple">Abraham Whipple</a> and an armed tender of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">British</a> Frigate <i>Rose</i>. The tender was chased aground and captured. Later in June, the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_General_Assembly" title="Rhode Island General Assembly">General Assembly</a> created the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Navy" title="American Navy">American Navy</a> when it commissioned the Sloops <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=USS_%27%27Providence%27%27_(1775)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="USS &lt;/i&gt;Providence&lt;i&gt; (1775) (page does not exist)">Katy</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Washington_(1776_row_galley)" title="USS Washington (1776 row galley)"><i>Washington</i></a>, armed with 24 guns and commanded by Abraham Whipple, who was promoted to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodore_(USN)" title="Commodore (USN)">Commodore</a>. Rhode Island was the first Colony to declare <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> from Britain on May 4, 1776.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-3"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Pelham Street in Newport was the first in America to be illuminated by gaslight in 1806.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-4"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The first strike in the United States in which women participated occurred in Pawtucket in 1824.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-5"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Watch_Hill,_Rhode_Island" title="Watch Hill, Rhode Island">Watch Hill</a> has the nation\'s oldest flying horses <a href="/wiki/Carousel" title="Carousel">carousel</a> that has been in continuous operation since 1850.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-6"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The motion picture machine (a machine showing animated pictures) was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patented" title="Patented">patented</a> in Providence on April 23, 1867.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-7"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The first lunch wagon in America was introduced in Providence in 1872.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-8"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The first nine-hole <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf course</a> in America was completed in Newport in 1890.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-9"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The first state health laboratory was established in Providence on September 1, 1894.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-10"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_State_House" title="Rhode Island State House">Rhode Island State House</a> was the first building with an all-<a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a> dome to be built in the United States (1895\xe2\x80\x931901).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-11"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The first automobile race on a track was held in Cranston on September 7, 1896.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-12"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup> The first automobile parade was held in Newport on September 7, 1899 on the grounds of Belcourt Castle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_146-13"><a href="#cite_note-history-146">[146]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The first <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> night game was held on November 6, 1929 at Providence\'s Kinsley Park. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago_Cardinals_(NFL,_1920%E2%80%9359)" title="Chicago Cardinals (NFL, 1920\xe2\x80\x9359)">Chicago (now Arizona) Cardinals</a> defeated the Providence Steam Roller 16\xe2\x80\x930.</p>\n<p>In 1980, Rhode Island became the first state to decriminalize prostitution indoors, but indoor prostitution was outlawed again in 2009; see <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Rhode_Island" title="Prostitution in Rhode Island">Prostitution in Rhode Island</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Miscellaneous_local_culture">Miscellaneous local culture</span></h3>\n<p>Rhode Island is nicknamed "The Ocean State", and the nautical nature of Rhode Island\'s geography pervades its culture. Newport Harbor, in particular, holds many pleasure boats. In the lobby of <a href="/wiki/T._F._Green_Airport" title="T. F. Green Airport">T. F. Green</a>, the state\'s main airport, is a large life-sized sailboat,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> and the state\'s license plates depict an ocean wave or a sailboat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Additionally, the large number of beaches in <a href="/wiki/Washington_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Washington County, Rhode Island">Washington County</a> lures many Rhode Islanders south for summer vacation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The state was notorious for organized crime activity from the 1950s into the 1990s when the <a href="/wiki/Patriarca_crime_family" title="Patriarca crime family">Patriarca crime family</a> held sway over most of New England from its Providence headquarters.</p>\n<p>Rhode Islanders developed a unique style of architecture in the 17th century called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stone-ender" title="Stone-ender">stone-ender</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Rhode Island is the only state to still celebrate <a href="/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day" title="Victory over Japan Day">Victory over Japan Day</a>. It is known locally as "VJ Day" or simply "Victory Day".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="1111" height="77" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg/220px-McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg/330px-McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg/440px-McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McCoy_Stadium_Pan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMcCoy Stadium where the Pawtucket Red Sox play baseball</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bryantvwestchester.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="809" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bryantvwestchester.jpg/220px-Bryantvwestchester.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bryantvwestchester.jpg/330px-Bryantvwestchester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bryantvwestchester.jpg/440px-Bryantvwestchester.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bryantvwestchester.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBryant University\'s Bulldogs Stadium</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MeadeStadium1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/MeadeStadium1.jpg/220px-MeadeStadium1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/MeadeStadium1.jpg/330px-MeadeStadium1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/MeadeStadium1.jpg/440px-MeadeStadium1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MeadeStadium1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nUniversity of Rhode Island\'s Meade Stadium and Ryan Center</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1884grays.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="301" data-file-width="448" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/1884grays.jpg/220px-1884grays.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/1884grays.jpg/330px-1884grays.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/1884grays.jpg/440px-1884grays.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1884grays.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n1884 Baseball Champion Providence Grays</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional">Professional</span></h4>\n<p>Rhode Island has two professional sports teams, both of which are top-level minor league affiliates for teams in Boston. The <a href="/wiki/Pawtucket_Red_Sox" title="Pawtucket Red Sox">Pawtucket Red Sox</a> baseball team of the <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">Triple-A</a> <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">International League</a> are an affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>. They play at <a href="/wiki/McCoy_Stadium" title="McCoy Stadium">McCoy Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pawtucket,_Rhode_Island" title="Pawtucket, Rhode Island">Pawtucket</a> and have won four league titles, the <a href="/wiki/Governors%27_Cup" title="Governors\' Cup">Governors\' Cup</a>, in 1973, 1984, 2012, and 2014. McCoy Stadium also has the distinction of being home to the <a href="/wiki/Longest_professional_baseball_game" title="Longest professional baseball game">longest professional baseball game</a> ever played \xe2\x80\x93 33 innings.</p>\n<p>The other professional minor league team is the <a href="/wiki/Providence_Bruins" title="Providence Bruins">Providence Bruins</a> <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team of the <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">American Hockey League</a>, who are an affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a>. They play in the <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts_Center" title="Dunkin\' Donuts Center">Dunkin\' Donuts Center</a> in Providence and won the AHL\'s <a href="/wiki/Calder_Cup" title="Calder Cup">Calder Cup</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_AHL_season" title="1998\xe2\x80\x9399 AHL season">1998\xe2\x80\x9399 AHL season</a>.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Providence_Reds" title="Providence Reds">Providence Reds</a> were a hockey team that played in the Canadian-American Hockey League (CAHL) between 1926 and 1936 and the American Hockey League (AHL) from 1936 to 1977, the last season of which they played as the Rhode Island Reds. The team won the Calder Cup in 1938, 1940, 1949, and 1956. The Reds played at the Rhode Island Auditorium, located on North Main Street in Providence, Rhode Island from 1926 through 1972, when the team affiliated with the New York Rangers and moved into the newly built Providence Civic Center. The team name came from the rooster known as the Rhode Island Red. They moved to New York in 1977 and, after multiple name changes, are now called the <a href="/wiki/Hartford_Wolf_Pack" title="Hartford Wolf Pack">Hartford Wolf Pack</a>.</p>\n<p>The Reds are the oldest continuously operating minor-league hockey franchise in North America, having fielded a team in one form or another since 1926 in the CAHL. It is also the only AHL franchise to have never missed a season. The AHL returned to Providence in 1992 in the form of the Providence Bruins.</p>\n<p>Before the great expansion of athletic teams all over the country, Providence and Rhode Island in general played a great role in supporting teams. The <a href="/wiki/Providence_Grays" title="Providence Grays">Providence Grays</a> won the first World Championship in baseball history in 1884. The team played their home games at the old Messer Street Field in Providence. The Grays played in the National League from 1878 to 1885. They defeated the New York Metropolitans of the American Association in a best of five game series at the Polo Grounds in New York. Providence won three straight games to become the first champions in major league baseball history. <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> played for the minor league Providence Grays of 1914 and hit his only official minor league home run for that team before being recalled by the Grays\' parent club, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Stockings</a>.</p>\n<p>The now-defunct professional football team the <a href="/wiki/Providence_Steam_Roller" title="Providence Steam Roller">Providence Steam Roller</a> won the 1928 NFL title. They played in a 10,000 person stadium called the Cycledrome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Providence_Steamrollers" title="Providence Steamrollers">Providence Steamrollers</a> played in the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Association_of_America" title="Basketball Association of America">Basketball Association of America</a> which became the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>.</p>\n<p>Rhode Island is also home to a top semi-professional soccer club, the <a href="/wiki/RI_Reds" title="RI Reds">Rhode Island Reds</a>, which compete in the National premier soccer league, in the fourth division of U.S. Soccer.</p>\n<p>Rhode Island is home to one top level non-minor league team, the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Rebellion" title="Rhode Island Rebellion">Rhode Island Rebellion</a> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> team, a semi-professional rugby league team that competes in the <a href="/wiki/USA_Rugby_League" title="USA Rugby League">USA Rugby League</a>, the Top Competition in the United States for the Sport of Rugby League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bridge_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bridge-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> The Rebellion play their home games at Classical High School in Providence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Collegiate_and_amateur_sports">Collegiate and amateur sports</span></h4>\n<p>There are four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> Division I schools in Rhode Island. All four schools compete in different conferences. The <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University Bears</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bryant_Bulldogs" title="Bryant Bulldogs">Bryant University Bulldogs</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Conference" title="Northeast Conference">Northeast Conference</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Providence_Friars" title="Providence Friars">Providence College Friars</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979\xe2\x80\x932013)">Big East Conference</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Rams" title="Rhode Island Rams">University of Rhode Island Rams</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic-10 Conference</a>. Three of the schools\' football teams compete in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Championship_Subdivision" title="Football Championship Subdivision">Football Championship Subdivision</a>, the second-highest level of <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> in the United States. Brown plays FCS football in the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a>, Bryant plays FCS football in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Conference" title="Northeast Conference">Northeast Conference</a>, and Rhode Island plays FCS football in the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">Colonial Athletic Association</a>. All four of the Division I schools in the state compete in an intrastate all-sports competition known as the <a href="/wiki/Ocean_State_Cup" title="Ocean State Cup">Ocean State Cup</a>, with Bryant winning the most recent cup in 2011\xe2\x80\x9312 academic year.</p>\n<p>From 1930 to 1983, <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America\'s Cup">America\'s Cup</a> races were sailed off Newport, and the extreme-sport <a href="/wiki/X_Games" title="X Games">X Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gravity_Games" title="Gravity Games">Gravity Games</a> were founded and hosted in the state\'s capital city.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Tennis_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Tennis Hall of Fame">International Tennis Hall of Fame</a> is in Newport at the Newport Casino, site of the first U.S. National Championships in 1881. The Hall of Fame and Museum were established in 1954 by James Van Alen as "a shrine to the ideals of the game".</p>\n<p>Rhode Island is also home to the headquarters of the governing body for youth rugby league in the United States, the American Youth Rugby League Association or AYRLA. The AYRLA has started the first-ever Rugby League youth competition in Providence Middle Schools, a program at the RI Training School, in addition to starting the first High School Competition in the USA in Providence Public High School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USARL.com_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-USARL.com-158">[158]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Registered_Historic_Places_in_Rhode_Island" title="List of Registered Historic Places in Rhode Island">List of Registered Historic Places in Rhode Island</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_(north_facade).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1680" data-file-width="2240" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_%28north_facade%29.jpg/220px-Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_%28north_facade%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_%28north_facade%29.jpg/330px-Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_%28north_facade%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_%28north_facade%29.jpg/440px-Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_%28north_facade%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhode_Island_State_Capitol_(north_facade).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_State_House" title="Rhode Island State House">Rhode Island State House</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Breakers_Newport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/The_Breakers_Newport.jpg/220px-The_Breakers_Newport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/The_Breakers_Newport.jpg/330px-The_Breakers_Newport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/The_Breakers_Newport.jpg/440px-The_Breakers_Newport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Breakers_Newport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/The_Breakers" title="The Breakers">The Breakers</a> mansion</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_State_House" title="Rhode Island State House">state capitol building</a> is made of white Georgian marble. On top is the world\'s fourth largest self-supported marble dome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> It houses the Rhode Island Charter granted by <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">King Charles II</a> in 1663, the Brown University charter, and other state treasures.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Baptist_Church_in_America" title="First Baptist Church in America">First Baptist Church of Providence</a> is the oldest Baptist church in the Americas, founded by Roger Williams in 1638.</p>\n<p>The first fully automated post office in the country is located in Providence. There are many historic mansions in the seaside city of Newport, including <a href="/wiki/The_Breakers" title="The Breakers">The Breakers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marble_House" title="Marble House">Marble House</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belcourt_Castle" title="Belcourt Castle">Belcourt Castle</a>. Also located there is the <a href="/wiki/Touro_Synagogue" title="Touro Synagogue">Touro Synagogue</a>, dedicated on December 2, 1763, considered by locals to be the first synagogue within the United States (see below for information on New York City\'s claim), and still serving. The synagogue showcases the religious freedoms that were established by Roger Williams, as well as impressive architecture in a mix of the classic colonial and Sephardic style. The <a href="/wiki/Newport_Casino" title="Newport Casino">Newport Casino</a> is a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmark</a> building complex that presently houses the <a href="/wiki/International_Tennis_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Tennis Hall of Fame">International Tennis Hall of Fame</a> and features an active grass-court tennis club.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Route_1A" title="Rhode Island Route 1A">Scenic Route 1A</a> (known locally as Ocean Road) is in <a href="/wiki/Narragansett,_Rhode_Island" title="Narragansett, Rhode Island">Narragansett</a>. "<a href="/wiki/The_Towers_(Narragansett,_Rhode_Island)" title="The Towers (Narragansett, Rhode Island)">The Towers</a>" is also located in Narragansett featuring a large stone arch. It was once the entrance to a famous Narragansett casino that burned down in 1900. The Towers now serve as an event venue and host the local Chamber of Commerce, which operates a tourist information center.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Newport_Tower_(Rhode_Island)" title="Newport Tower (Rhode Island)">Newport Tower</a> has been hypothesized to be of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viking" title="Viking">Viking</a> origin, although most experts believe that it was a Colonial-era windmill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Rhode_Island" title="List of people from Rhode Island">List of people from Rhode Island</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li><img alt="" data-file-height="209" data-file-width="375" height="9"
